Polymorphisms found in the genomic flanking regions were used to identify the species of origin. <i>dTph1</i> elements were identified in a <i>P. axillaris</i> population using a modification of the methodology described in <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nplants201674#MOESM9">Supplementary Note 3</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Whole-genome duplication, tandem duplications and gene family analysis</h3><p>Whole-genome collinear analysis was performed using SynMap and microsynteny analysis were performed using GEvo in the comparative genomics platform, CoGe<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Lyons, E. &amp; Freeling, M. How to usefully compare homologous plant genes and chromosomes as DNA sequences. Plant J. 53, 661–673 (2008)." href="/articles/nplants201674#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d19403e3473">42</a></sup>. See <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nplants201674#MOESM9">Supplementary Note 5</a>.</p><p>The gene family analysis included <i>Solanum lycopersicum</i>, <i>S. tuberosum</i>, <i>Nicotiana benthamiana</i> and <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> protein sets using BlastP (v2.2.27)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Altschul, S. F. et al. Gapped BLAST and PSI-BLAST: a new generation of protein database search programs. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 3389–3402 (1997)." href="/articles/nplants201674#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d19403e3495">40</a></sup> on an all-versus-all comparison and grouping the genes into families with OrthoMCL, v2.0.8. See <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nplants201674#MOESM9">Supplementary Note 4</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Small RNA sequencing and analysis</h3><p>Total RNA was purified and small RNA libraries were prepared and sequenced and analysed following the methods described in <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nplants201674#MOESM9">Supplementary Note 9</a>. Annotation and identification was performed using Perl scripts, mirDeep-P (v1.3; <a href="http://sourceforge.net/projects/mirdp/">http://sourceforge.net/projects/mirdp/</a>), Bowtie (v1.0.1) and CLCbio, based on identity to miRNAs in <i>Arabidopsis</i> and Solanaceae spp. Secondary structures of pre-miRNAs were predicted with RNAfold (<a href="http://rna.tbi.univie.ac.at/cgi-bin/RNAfold.cgi">http://rna.tbi.univie.ac.at/cgi-bin/RNAfold.cgi</a>). MiRNA target genes were predicted using TargetFinder (v1.6). See <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nplants201674#MOESM9">Supplementary Note 9</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20"><i>Petunia hybrida</i> transcripts comparison</h3><p><i>Petunia hybrida</i> (accessions Mitchell, R27 and R143) reads were mapped to the <i>P. axillaris</i> genome (v1.6.2) using Bowtie2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Fast gapped-read alignment with Bowtie 2. Nature Methods 9, 357–359 (2012)." href="/articles/nplants201674#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d19403e3551">35</a></sup>. SNPs were called using FreeBayes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Garrison, E. &amp; Marth, G. Haplotype-based variant detection from short-read sequencing. Preprint at 
                    http://arxiv.org/abs/1207.3907
                    
                   (2012)." href="/articles/nplants201674#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d19403e3555">36</a></sup> and annotated using Snpeff<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Cingolani, P. et al. A program for annotating and predicting the effects of single nucleotide polymorphisms, SnpEff. Fly 6, 80–92 (2014)." href="/articles/nplants201674#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d19403e3559">37</a></sup>. Exons and genes were assigned to <i>P. axillaris</i> or <i>P. inflata</i> based in the SNP data using a Perl script. Five categories were used: Homozygous <i>P. axillaris</i>; Homozygous <i>P. inflata</i>; Heterozygous <i>P. axillaris/P. inflata</i>; Homozygous <i>P. axillaris</i>/<i>P. inflata</i> and unclear assignment. Homozygous SNPs for the genes with exons from both species were confirmed aligning <i>P. hybrida</i> EST using Exonerate (v2.2 l; <a href="http://www.ebi.ac.uk/about/vertebrate-genomics/software/exonerate">http://www.ebi.ac.uk/about/vertebrate-genomics/software/exonerate</a>). Gene Set Enrichment Analysis (GSEA) was performed using the Bioconductor package TopGO (v2.22.0; <a href="http://bioconductor.org/packages/topGO/">http://bioconductor.org/packages/topGO/</a>). See <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nplants201674#MOESM9">Supplementary Note 6</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Gene data mining</h3><p>The specific identification of genes for <i>P. axillaris</i> and <i>P. inflata</i> genomes for colour and scent, root-specific pathways, self-incompatibility and circadian clock was performed through a BlastN/BlastP sequence homology search. Blast GUI, JBrowser (<a href="http://jbrowse.org/">http://jbrowse.org/</a>) and WebApollo (<a href="http://genomearchitect.org/">http://genomearchitect.org/</a>) were installed in a server to search and manually curate the gene structures of the identified genes. See <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nplants201674#MOESM9">Supplementary Notes 7, 8 and 10–12</a>.</p><p>The <i>P. axillaris</i> and <i>P. inflata</i> genome sequences are available on the Sol Genomics Network (SGN) at <a href="https://solgenomics.net/organism/Petunia_axillaris/genome">https://solgenomics.net/organism/Petunia_axillaris/genome</a> and <a href="https://solgenomics.net/organism/Petunia_inflata/genome">https://solgenomics.net/organism/Petunia_inflata/genome</a>, respectively.</p></div></div></section>
